While the expected impacts are well-documented in the literature for other countries, it will still be
importantthat the GoC continue with its results-based management strategy and monitor the long-run
impacts of its policies. Additionally, several initiatives, such as the expansion of apprenticeships, the
creation of a unified databaseof beneficiaries, or the access of informalsector workers to the public social
security system, are less well documentedinthe general literature andmerit deeper evaluations. The Bank
andthe MSPhave beendiscussingthe needfor such studies andidenufylnghowandwhento incorporate
these intothe MSP's evaluationagenda.

PARTICIPATION
As discussed above, Colombiahas anactive civil societythat interacts with alllevels of Government. The
keypolicies supported under the LaRSDPLI11inallsectors have beenthe subject of debate inmanyfora
(see Annex IV for examples). Additionally, the DEPP-DNP and the MSP have been undertaang a
systematic effort to improve the communication between civil society and policymakers at the national
level. While oversight of the National Development Plan has become systematized via the National
PlanningCouncil, the DEPP-DNPhas beenexperimenting withprocessesto opendebate onother topics
to groups with additional interests; the proposedLaRSDPLI11supports this process, as does the Social
SafetyNet InvestmentLoan, at the level of the Ministryof Social Protectionandthe forthcoming M&E
operation with the DNP.

SUPERVISION
The rich social and labor programthat the GoCand the Bankhave been developing over the period of
the Uribe Administrationis the result of anactive andfrequent dialogue. Over this period, the Bankhas
had regular interaction with the client reg+       the progress of implementation of the labor and social
program, monitoringandmanagingresults, andstrategizing for the next roundof reforms. The ICRs for
the PLaRSSAzs showed greater progress than expected when the operations were prepared and, if the
riskspresentedbelowdo notrealize themselves, the same is expectedforthis single tranche operation.

Interms of thisparticular operation, the multi-sectoralteamwouldcontinuetoworkwiththe current and
new Administration's DNP, MSP, MEN, ICBF, SEN& and Ministry of Finance in supervision of the
proposed operation to assess implementationof the prior actions, results of actions, andcompliance with
the fiduciary responsibilities. Given the completion of the current Government in August 2006, the
formation of a new Cabinet, andthe end of the proposed operation for early 2007, supervision activities
will focus onsupportingthe continuationof the LaRSDPLI11policies duringthe transitionphase.

These supervision activities will, as is customary for the Bank's social and labor team w o r k with
Colombia, take place in the context of supervision of a larger labor and social program including the


                                                     44

implementation of the TAL, supervision of the Social Safety Net operation, preparation of the M&E
operation, andthe on-goingESWprogram.

FIDUCIARYASPECTS
FinancialManagement.

Colombia's fiduciary environment for LaRSDPL I11is considered adequate. Inrecent pan Colombia
has made important progress in its Public Financial Management (PFM) systems and improved
transparency inpublic finance due to reforms incritical areas also with the assistance of the WorldBank
andthe IADB. Importantinitiatives include adoptionof the PublicAdministrationRenovationProgram
(PRAP), which includes anti-corruption andfiscal responsibilitymeasures.111

The government that took office inAugust 2002 has also improved the administration of publiclyowned
banks, clarified responsibilities for managing expenditures among different levels of government, and
introduced modern accounting concepts andprocedures. These initiatives were supported bythe rollout
of newinformation systems coveringthe budget andlocalgovernment finances, as well as the monitoring
of publicprocurement.

The Bank, incoordinationwith the IADB, carried out a CFAA for Colombia in2003-2004. The CFAA
was coordinated with the IBRD's PER and 2003 Fiscal and InstitutionalAdjustment Loans (FIAL), and
the IMF's May 2003 Fiscal Transparency Report on Standards and Codes @OSq,             which cover other
aspects of Colombia's fiscal management. Officialdelivery of CFAAto Government took place inApril
2005. This diagnostic review pointedto a series of importantadvances but also remainingweaknesses in
publicsectormanagement inColombia.

The country has made progress in modemizing and automating its PFM and information systems,
especially with regard to the Integrated Financial Management System (SIIF) implementation. This
progress has been uneven, however, and the government lacks an integrated vision of an overall PFM
system To remedy this shortcoming, the Inter-Governmental Policy and Information Management
Committee was created.112 These problems anda lackof accountabilityfor results have limitedthe q d t y
andeffectiveness of public financialmanagement. Budgetformulationis alsofragmented, whichprevents
the budget from being used as a strategic governance tool. These problems have made PFM
responsibilities diffuse, and duplication and overlapping agency responsibilities prevent the government
fromsetting andachieving clearPFMgoals.

Planned revisions to the Organic Budget Code should be used to strengthen budget programming and
control by establishing a new mechanism to coordinate expenditures across a medium-termframework
that takes into account financial programminggoals andanticipatedresource availabilities andthroughthe
implementation of the single treasury account. Throughpresidential decree No. 4730 of December 2005,
articles of the Organic budget Code related to the budget system, budget cycle and budget for public
enterprises will be effective during2006 and2007.

The Treasury Directorate's S I F - which includes budget, treasury and accounting modules- registers
and incorporates timely and reliable information on the expenditure process. Inearly 2006, GoCM y
implemented direct payments to suppliers, improvingthe management of cash on handandinbanks and
increasing transparency of the system In addition the government has developed the SINERGIA to
evaluate the results of public expenditures, and begun implementing a program to strengthen and
integrate the financial information systems for local government bodies. ( P n p i i p ad Farkllacimslto
S i s m & I $ dFkmima T d ,FOSIT.) Additional programs aim to track procurement and
otherfinancial information.

  Inrecent years, the government has made importantprogress inbuildingits debt management capacity
  throughtechnical and institutionalstrengthening of the Finance Ministryand implementation of a new
  public debt information system The 2003 Fiscal Responsibility and Transparency Law strengthened
  regulation of sub-national government indebtedness, although this still requires attention. Furthermore,
  the government has put inplace an informationsystem to register contingent liabilities on national, sub
  national, and public works contracts. The system includes the creation and operation of contractual
  contingency funds. All operations are inthe public domain, and informationon debt is published on a
  regular basis.

  Under the 1991 Constitution, fiscal control is vested inthe external and internal control systems. The
  Comptroller General, Colombia's supreme audit institution, andthe regional comptrollers are incharge of
 external audits, and each public entity has an internalcontrol unit.The fiscal control system also includes
 the Auditor General, who is responsible for supervising administrative management of the regional
 comptroller offices. IADB is supporting a multi-year project to modernize the Comptroller General's
  Office andimprove its audit capacitybughtrainingandimprovedinformationtechnologysystems.

 Based on the CFAA conclusions, Colombia's country fiduciary risk rating is moderate. The CFAA
 examinedthe risks posed byweaknesses inpublic financial management systems, the way inwhich public
  resources flow inthe system, andthe strength andreliabilityof the control framework applied to financial
 transa~tions.113

 The administration of projects financed with Bank and IADB resources has generally been satisfactory,
 although government fiscal adjustments have sometimes delayed counterpart resources, andrestrictions in
 expenditure andcash flow management.

 PFM improvements already under way in Colombia or triggered by the CFAA action plan
 recommendations, andthe implementation of the Bank-financedPublic Financial Management Project I1
  (MAFP Iz), are allconsistent with the Government's long-termfocus to improve andmodernizepublic
 Sector management andare expected to contribute reasonable fiduciaryassurance as the Bankincreases its
 development policylendmg.

 The Bankhas reviewed the UIZF's latest assessment of the borrower's Central Bank, which shows that the
 control environment of the BdR is satisfactory. No remedial actions are necessary interms of foreign
 exchangefiduciaryarrangements

Procurement. The Bankjointlywith IADBcompleted the CPARfor Colombia inJune 2005. The report
provides a number of recommendations for the Government to improve procurement performance, inter
 alia, strengthening the regulatory body, reforming and modernizingthe procurement law, accelerating the
 implementation of a modern e-procurement system, improvingthe procurement planning tools, carrying
 out selected cost efficiency studies, adopting government procurementstandard biddingdocuments and
establishing a certification program for government officials. With respect to the procurement

DISBURSEMENT
LoanAmount andDisbursement. The operation is proposed for a $200 d o n . The loanwould be in
the form of a fixed-spread, US-dollar-denominated loan, and made to the Republic of Colombia. The
proposed LaRSDPL I11will follow the Bank's disbursement procedures for development policyl e n d q .
The untied financial support will be disbursed against satisfactory implementation of the development
policy lending programand not tied to any specific purchases. The loan would cover the one-tranche
LaRSDPLIII.

The Bankwill disburse the loanproceeds into an account of the CentralBankdenominated inUS dollars.
The GoCrecords an equivalent amount of local currency inthe PFMsystem and the USD become part
of the officialforeign exchangereserves. The CentralBankwillimmediatelycredit the disbursedamounts
to the Ministryof Finance's TreasuryAccount, thus becomingavailable to finance budgetedexpenditures.
Withina week of the disbursement, the Ministrywillaccordinglyprovide the Bankwrittenconfirmation
of the transaction. If, after deposit inthe CentralBank, loanproceeds are nottreated as described above,
the Bankwillrequire the Governmentto promptlyrefund the disallowed amount.

The administration of this Loanwillbe the responsibility of the MHCP.

Fiscal Impact. The programis within the CAS mandated FY 2007 limit for lendingto Colombia. The
reformprogramis intended to increase coverage andqualityof social expenditures without increasing the
totalbudget envelope, throughbetter allocation anduse of resources, as discussedinSectionV above,

ENVIRONMENTALASPECTS
FollowingOP 8.60, the operation was reviewed for any potentialeffects relating to the environment,
forest, and naturalresources. As this loan focuses on strengthening the institutions, policyframework,
and qualityof social protection inColombia, it has been determined that the operation is not likelyto
have anysignificant effects on the environment.

In the framework of the CAS, the Bank recognizes and supports the Colombian Government in
strengthening the environmental sustainability of its development program, as is evidenced by the
Programmatic Development Policy loanfor Sustainable Development approved bythe Bank's Boardon
June 2005. The LaRSDPLI11team is providinginputs to the health-related actions inthe Development
Policy loan for Sustainable Development, and collaborating on understandq the implications for
environmentallyinduced illnesses on the demand for health care.          The MSP also recognizes the
connection between the environment and health care, and has an on-goingdialogue with the Ministryof
the Environment.

RISKS AND RISKMITIGATION
Inthe PLaRSSAL11,two categories of riskwere identified generalrisksfromthe economic andpolitical
                                                           -
situation and labor- and social-specific risks emerging from the management of the reform program
supportedbythis program Whilethese risks still exist, theyare less relatedto the implementation of the

                                                    47

program and more a threat to sustainability of an aggressive reform programthat may be under new
management bythe end of 2006. A thirdriskcan be added: transitionalrisks as the re-elected President
finishes this administration andforms a newCabinet.

The risks to the success of this operation are moderate if well managed. The risks identified inthe earlier
PLaRSSALs, outcomes of those risks, their status for the proposed operation and sustainability of the
reformprogram, and actions bythe GoCand the Bankto mitigate the risks are presented inAnnex V I
andsummarizedbelow.

Gerreral kks, The general risks that have been an issue throughout the PLaRSSAL series, though well
managed, continue to be anissue:

     0   The violence associated with illegal drug activity may divert resources and attention from the
          government while aggravating the social situation. W        e the Government's aggressive campaign
         has resulted ina decreaseinkidnappings by50 percent, homicides by33 percent, guerrilla attacks
         onmunicipalities by80 percent andnewdisplaced families by33 percent between2003 and2004,
         and demobilization and reintegrationefforts have resulted in18,000 ex-combatants returned to
         civilian life, the risks still remain. Violent groups increased attacks during the electoral period
          (thoughless so than inpreviousyears), butthe Government continues its peaceefforts, withthe
         support of the UNDP, USAID, and, increasingly, with the support of the Bank's new "peace
         pillar" to the CAS.

     0   The need for tight fiscal constraints could affect the financing of the reforms. The failure of
         the 2003 Referendum to reign-inpublic spendmg was worrisome, but the GoC has advanced
         other notable reforms to address the fiscal situation: pension reform and careful evaluation of
         the law for transferring resources to the territories, the two issues highlightedbythe IMFintheir
         recent review.114 Economic growth, renewedprivate sector investment, andcontinuous favorable
         assessments bythe IMFsuggest that the overallfiscal riskis being managed. The Bankcontinues
         to support the Government's efforts through fiscal and financial reform support as well as
         technical and operational assistance to the competitiveness and free trade agenda. Additionally,
         the Bank and the IADB are supporting a studyto assist the GoC inidentifying a sub-national
         fundingformulato updateLaw715 in2008.115

     0   External political and economic shocks are an increasing threat to the well-functioning
         Colombian economy. Political events inseveral nelghboring countries, increasing oilprices that
         have given new power to some actors, and the competing interests inthe Free Trade of the
         Americas negotiations may affect the fiscal, political, and macroeconomic situation of Colombia.
         The GoCis mitigatingthese risks bymaintainingfriendly relations with all nelghbors and creating
         its own sub-regional alliances. The Bank      is supporting the GoCthrough assistance on moving
         forwardthe competitiveness andinstitutionalreformagendas

       This risk has been mitigated through a marketingcampaign demonstrating the benefits of the

       social sectors. The Bank has supported these efforts by technical and financial support to the
       impact evaluation and monitoring activities and the policy reforms to improve efficiency in
       service provision.

   0   The h n c i a l viability of the health reform could be a riskto the fiscal health of the country.
       The health reformhas been expensive, since the phasing out of the old system necessarily lags
       behind the implementation of the new system to avoid disrupting the provisionof health care.
       This process has taken longer than hoped, which has threatened the viability of the reform
       process at times; some discussion has arisen about abandoning the new system and returningto
       the old, inefficient system simply with the objective of curbing the short-term costs. The MSP
       has undertaken actions to increase the efficiency of own expenditures to make this transition
       process less painful reducing double affiliation in the program, r e s t r u c m hospitals for

TRANSLA'IIONINTOENGLISH- LETIEROFDEVELOPMENTPOLICY




                                                                                 BogotB, May 17,2006



Mr. PAULWOLFOWITZ
President
THEWORLD BANK
Washington, D.C.


Dear Mr. Wolfowitz:


The Administration of President Alvaro Uribe V6lez continues to be completely involved in and
committed to the implementationof a program of social reforms over the 2003-2006 period, which is
being supported by the World Bank. These reforms, which are part of an ongoing quest for
macroeconomic stabilityand greater integrationintothe world economy, to which the Governmenthas
firmly committed, includes the implementationand continuation of a series of reformsthat also have
beenendorsed bythe multilateralcredit institutions.

In this context, the new Labor and Social Reform Project has been one of the most importanttools to
continue effective implementationof reforms begun under the First and Second ProgrammaticLabor
Reform and Social StructuralAdjustment Programs. Indeed, the project will support the Government
in continuing and consolidating many of the initiatives that were planned and implemented by the
current Administration as part of the National Development Plan. From the beginning of this
Administration, the social sectors have played an important role in a strategy -on par with fiscal and
economic stability-to reducepovertyand unemploymentthat haveaffectedthe countryin recentyears,
a strategy through which the present Administration has proudly achieved significant progress. The
Government's highest priorities have been providing internal security, constructing a more equitable
society and encouraging economic recovery. To achieve these priorities, it has been necessary to
continuesupportingthe social sectors, bothfinancially and politically.

It is very important to the Governmentthat the Bank's financing instrumentsevolve on a par with the
social policies being carried out by the country. For this reason, it is appropriate that the Labor and
Social Reform Project is signed under the modality of a Developmental Policy Loan (DPL). It is
through this loan that the World Bank, in fiscal year 2005, has supported the country in the
establishment of a program of social sector reforms that have been carried out with the goal of
providing the Government of Colombia with the necessary tools to strengthen the sectors, and in
particular, to increase quality and coverage of services in health, education, labor and social
assistance. The strengthening of the social protection system has served as the basis for recent
progress, and the technical and financial support of the World Bank has played a fundamental role in
thesetransformations.

In addition, the Government has continued to support projects complementary to the social sector
credit through the implementation of sub-projects in the areas of education, social assistance, and
monitoringand evaluation, amongothers.

The support of a multilateral bank, and specifically of the World Bank, has been very helpful to the
social progress initiated during the current Administration. The new operation, now classified as a
DevelopmentalPolicy Loan, will further help to strengthen increase the efficiencyand guarantee the
sustainabilityof the actions and policies taken within the social sectors. The above demonstratesthat
the Government is extremely satisfied with the ongoing reforms and programs.                Indeed, the


                                                  79

  Government confirms its commitment to improving the quality of life for its populationwith a program
  based on equityand assistance, an approachthat the newAdministrationis expectedto share.

  This policy letter, as a complement to those presented for the previous two reform projects, provides
  the Bank with an update on each of the relevant policy areas, as well as a summary of the new
  initiativesthat are being implementedinthe social sectors.

  The Government is very pleased to bring this Administration to a close having achieved a number of
  results and consolidationsof different programsand policiesof highsocial impact.

  Finally, the country is committed to the program that is presented in this document and welcomes and
  approves the technical and financial support of the World Bank. The Governmentappreciates a timely
  consideration by the Executive Directors of the World Bank. This loan for the development of labor
  and social policies in the amount of US$200 million for the year 2006, will continue the spirit of the
  policiesand actions carried out under the Firstand Second PLaRSSALprojects.

  Sincerely,



  Originalsigned                                            Originalsigned

1. ENSURING MACROECONOMICSTABILITY

1. In recent years, the Colombian Government has designed and executed a successful economic
program that aims at strengthening public finances, the results for which were first observed during
2004 and deepened in 2005. The main objectives of this program are the stabilization of the public
debt and the gradual reduction of the fiscal deficit so as to guarantee the structural sustainabilityof
publicfinances, focusing on decreasingcurrentand futureexpenses and increasingincome. The fiscal
situation has steadily improved, as evidenced by the following: in 2004 the consolidated public sector
deficit was only 1.3% of GDP and in 2005 the country achieved fiscal balance, greatly surpassingthe
goals agreeduponwith the InternationalMonetary Fund.

2. During the first six months of 2005, the Congressof the Republic approved several laws that have
contributedto the strengtheningof the Government's economic program.This has generated national
and international confidence in the economy, thus assuring macroeconomic stability. The approved
laws guarantee a decrease in the fiscal risks faced by the country and greater market transparency.
Therefore, it has been possible to generate a favorable atmosphere for both national and foreign
investment,whichwill assuresustainablegrowth of the Colombian economy.

3. The Pensions Legislative Act (Acto Legislativo de Pensiones)was modified to give viability and
financial sustainability to the public sector pension regime, which is the main fiscal risk facing the
country.Among the most important items approved in June 2005 are the following: establishmentof a
maximumamountfor pensionsto be paid by the NationalBudget (25 minimumwages, legallyvalid as
of July 31, 2010); eliminationof the exceptionaland specialpensionregimes,with the exceptionof the
public sector workforce (validfrom July 31, 2010); eliminationof the "14th Month Salary" (mesada 14)
for new pensioners,with exception of people who would receive a pension equal to or less than three
monthly minimum legal wages between July 31, 2011 and the anticipation of the conclusion of the
transition of Law 100 on July 31 of 2010. This reform would result in a savings of 20.1% of present
value GDP within 50 years, which when added to the savings reached by the enactment of Laws 797
and 860 of 2003, would result in total savingsof 22.7% of GDP.

4. At the same time, the Securities Market Law (Ley del Mercadode Valores, Law 964- July 8, 2005)
and the Legal Stability Law (Ley de Estabilidad Juridica, Law 963- July 8, 2005) guarantee market
transparencyand generatea favorableatmosphereto attract investmentto the country.The Securities
Market Law modernizesthe regulation of this market. In this way, market activity is professionalized,
supervisionof the market is strengthened, and clear rulesfor market are established. Conversely, the
LegalStabilityLaw creates the concept of "legallystablecontracts"which aims to ensurethat investors
who sign said contracts are not harmed or adverselyaffected in any way by changes in the normsthat
havebeen identifiedin thesecontracts.

5. The changes in Colombian legislationguaranteedthe continuationof a healthy fiscal policy as well
as market transparency. This has led to a significant decrease in the Government's interest rates on
debt payments in the first months of the year. Nevertheless,this has not been the only thing on which
the country has been working. In light of the firm intentionto increasethe country's economic growth,
the negotiationsfor the FreeTrade Agreementwith the UnitedStateswere finalized, with the objective
to increaseboth exports and greater foreign investmentinthe countryin the upcomingyears.

6. The implementationof all these changes in the legislation and the development of the economic
plan to fortify public finances had the desired effect and it was in 2005 that Colombia reapedthe fruits
of its labor.GDP growth of 5.1% in 2005 is evidenceof the significant resultsachieved (aboveaverage
growth for Latin America). Inflation was also favorable at 4.85%. This growth is mostly due to
increaseddemand within the country, which was supported by an increase in home purchases, given
the improved economic conditions and the greater confidence in the private sector. Also, investment
(which grew 29% in 2005) has been one of the most dynamic elements of domestic demand. On the
other hand, an increase in Government demand along with exports also contributed positively to the
growthof the GDP.

7. In general, the positiveeconomic developmentexperienced by Colombia in 2005 was supportedby
growth in all sectors of the economy, and was based on the increase in domestic demand, especially
of privateconsumption and investment.All of this took placewithin an environmentof providinggreater

                                                    83

security of private property, which has promoted confidence in the country. In fact, the sustained
increase in the investment rate during the last few years enables one to be optimistic about the
medium- term growth of the Colombian economy. Thus, the positive results of economic activity have
been reflected in an improvement of fiscal indicators, a reduction in debt, and in a reduction of the
perceptionof risk by investors. This has resulted in an important reductionin the Country's financing
costs in internationalfinancial markets.


II.SOCIAL PROTECTIONSYSTEM

A. Structureand Operationof the Social Protectionand Social SecuritySystem

8. As established by the NationalDevelopment Plan, the creation of a more equitablesociety must be
one of the foundations of developmentpolicy, for which threefundamentalchallengesexist: i) increase
the efficiencyof social expendituresso that moreresourcestranslate into better results; ii) improvethe
targeting of expenditures so that resourcesgo to those who most need them; and iii) consolidatethe
social protectionsystemso that economiccrisesdo not adverselyaffect the mostvulnerablegroups.

9. Social protection in Colombia was characterized by a series of organizations without common
objectives, uncoordinated amongst themselves and with a large number of fragmented and
overlapping programs. Although the social security system, through Law 100 of 2003, expanded the
delivery of traditional social services, it did not create the necessary tools for social protection and
assistance, particularlytemporaryprogramsthat mitigatethe adverseeffects of economiccriseson the
poorest groups. Such programs consist of those addressing child malnutrition, helping to keep
children and youth in school, training the unemployed for integration or re-integration into the labor
market,and providinglarge-scaleemergency employment.

10. It is within this context that the present Administration undertook aggressively a strategy to
restructure the State, which has permitted the creation of the institutional structure that allows for
greater integrationamong organizations,policy coherenceand a reduction in the duplicationof efforts.
In particular, this restructuring created the Ministry of Social Protection, which manages both the
designof and follow-up on social policy,as well as oversightof the mainimplementingorganizations.

11. As it was expressed in policy letters for the first and second PLaRSSAL projects, the objective in
creating the Social Protection System (SPS) is to reduce the risks faced by the population during
economic shocks and to help the poor confront the associated risks. Similarly, the SPS aims to
coordinate the policies of the State and to confront the adverse effects of poverty and vulnerability,
protect the most vulnerable through the coordination and execution of social programs accompanied
byfinancingmechanismsthat guaranteea timely response.

12. The first step to put the conceptual framework of the SPS into operation was to create the legal
and regulatoryframework on which the institutionsthat are part of the system could rely.The legislative
agenda at the beginningof this Administrationwas geared specificallyto regulatorymatters; Congress
approved the labor and pension reform in December of 2002. The Labor Reform law allowed for
modifications of existing labor codes, defined the Social Protection System, and included norms to
supportthe use and extensionof social protection.

13. In parallel, the Ministry of Social Protection (MPS) was created as result of the merging of the
former Ministries of Labor and Health. The responsibility of the Ministry is to design and coordinate
policies under the social protection strategy. This strategy encompasses the following areas: public
health, training, labor policies and standards, interventionsto reduce child labor and disability policies.
Indeed, the Ministry is the decision-making entity for policymaking and inter-institutional coordination
betweenthe organizationsthat are partof the SPS.117




11'The institutionsthat make upthe Social ProtectionSystem arethe Ministry of Social Protection, ICBF,the
Compensation Fund, ISS, SENA, the Pension Fund,the SocialProtectionFund, SUPERSUBSIDIO, INSand
INVIMAamong others.

                                                    84

14. In light of the above, a series of complementary actions have designed and put in place to
institutionally restructure the existing social protection organizations (SENA, Family Compensation
Associations, ICBF, etc.) and to create the legal and conceptual framework for the SPS, which is
describedbelow.

B. Advancesin the Implementationof the Social ProtectionSystem

1. LaborReform

15. Some time ago, the Government, academics and others in society showed evidence of the
necessity to undertake labor market reforms in Colombia, which they argued was fundamental to
improvingthe dynamicsofjob creationand complementaryto the recoveryof economicgrowth.

16, Above all, what the country now faces, and will continueto face in years to come, is an economic
environment that is totally different from that which the country faced 10 or 20 years ago. Companies
and employees alike are faced with new economic surroundings that require much more agile
mechanismsof adaptationthat will not put the country's competitivenessand, as a result,job creation,
at risk. Therefore, additionalpolicy instruments,besidessimply macroeconomicpolicy, are neededso
that the country can attain socially acceptable unemployment rates. Among these instruments, the
updatingof the labor code was one of the most importantchallengesface by this government.Among
other things, such reformswere necessaryso that the country could take advantageof the business
and employment growth potentialthat will be made possible by the free trade agreement undertaken
with the UnitedStates.


LegalStandards

17. The current Government was conscious of this necessity. For this reason, the government
undertook responsibility, from the beginning, to improve the flexibility of the labor market. This
commitment was stated in the Development plan "Towards a Communal State", in spite of clearly
understanding how difficult it would be to pass a law of this nature in the Congress of the Republic.
Fortunately,the proposedlegislationwas passedby bothchambersof Congress, and is today a Law of
the Republic(Law789 of 2002).

18. Part of the success in passingthe new law was that it went beyond the scope of previousefforts,
which focused on proposingreformssolelywithin the scopeof labor standardsand regulations,and did
not take into account the associated social costs, especially in countries like Colombia where we do
not have consolidated social protection mechanisms to reduce the risks associated with
unemployment. From the beginning, it was considered necessary to create an institutional structure
that facilitated risk sharing and an improvement in the employabilityof the country's work force. It is
thus that Law 789 (Labor Reform Law) and Law 797 (Pension Reform Law) became part of the legal
frameworkthat will supportthe strengtheningColombia'ssocialprotectionsystem.

19. From the beginning,the new Labor Reform Law (789 of 2002) was designedwith three phases of
implementation. From the moment the law was approved, all the new articles that update labor
relations (Articles 25, 26, 27, 28 and 29) became legally valid for all newly hired workers. Duringthe
second phase these stipulations became valid for the people who were already working prior to
approvalof the law. Inthe last phase, the NationalGovernmentcarriedout a planallowingit to regulate
mostof Law 789 of 2002.

20. One of the high-priority provisions for the Government was the regulation of Article 13, which
exonerates companiesfrom the temporary payment of payroll taxes if they hire new employeeswho
belongto vulnerablegroups of the population.This was shaped by Decree2286 of 2003, in which the
conditionsof accreditationand the proceduresfor the exonerationof the paymentof payrolltaxes were
also established.At the same time, the Law created the Fund for the Promotion of Employmentand
Protection of the Unemployed(Fondo para el Foment0 del Empleo y Protecci6n al Desemp1eado)by
means of Articles 6 and 11, which were regulated through Decrees 2340, 3450 of 2003, 827 of 2003
and 586 of 2004.


                                                    85

21. Additionally, the regulationand use of the learningcontractas an instrumentto reducelabor costs,
facilitate labor relations and give greater employment opportunities to youth took shape with the
approval of Decree 933 of 2003, which regulates Articles 30 to 38 of the law. On the other hand,
through article 40 of Law 789 of 2003 an EnterpriseFund (Fondo Emprender)was createdto serve as
a special accountassignedto SENAwith the objectiveof financing businessinitiativesto be developed
by apprentices, businessmenor professionals,and made law by Decree934 of 2003.

22. Estimationsof employment used to justify the law assumed that in the beginning the effect of the
new legislation was going to be greater and as years passed, its effects would gradually diminish. In
particular, it was expected that in the first two years (2003 and 2004) 318,000 new jobs would be
generated by the reform. However, it wasn't clear how these jobs would be generated, that is to say
exactly how manyjobs would be generated in each year was unclear. For this reason, the analysis of
the real effects of the change in legal regulations must be made simultaneously between the years
previous to the change (2001-2002) compared to what happened in the years following the change
(2003-2005).

23. As of 2003, the labor market began a critical recovery process with respect to what had been
observed in previous years. Employment levels rose from 16.5 million in the third quarter of 2002 to
17.6 million in the same period of 2004 and 18.2 million in 2005, representingthe creation of 1.1 and
1.6 million jobs, respectively. This unusual rate in the generation of jobs (mainly of good quality) and
the improvement of other labor variables is an indication of the effect of the reform that cannot be
attributedexclusivelyto the economic recovery.

24. If we look at the dynamics of job creation according to business size for the 13 main cities, we
observe that on average between 2001 and 2002 compared to years 2003 and 2005, 564,546 jobs
were created, of which 70.7% were created in the laborer or clerk occupational positions, which are
considered positions of good quality.118 Additionally, 59% of these new jobs were created in
companieswith 11 and more people, which is to say in the medium to large sized companies, exactly
where it was hoped that the labor reform would have its greatest influence.This larger number of new
jobs in large companies is mostly concentrated in formal occupational sectors (95%), which concurs
with the greater number of peoplecovered by social security in the last two years.

25. Additionally, different independent investigations have estimated the impact of the reform before
and after its implementation, using empirical estimations that compare variables associated with
employment, such as hiring, under-employmentand wages. These studies were: byAlejandro Gaviria
(2004) and Jairo NLiAez(2004), both researchers at the Universityof the Andes; Hugo Lopez (2004) of
the Cide Corporation; and Verc5nica Amarante, along with Rodrigo Arim (2005), both of whom are
Paraguayanresearchers.

26. Of these studies, three found that the reform had positiveand significant effects on such variables
related to employment and unemployment such as: greater demand for employment, increase in the
probability of finding a job, increase in the duration of the job (more stability) and decrease in the
duration of unemployment.Additionally, the studies proved the effect of the reform on some variables
of job quality, where three of the investigationsfound evidence infavor of a substantial improvementin
labor conditions measured by a greater probability of being employed by the formal sector and
decrease in informal employment. Also, the only study that researched under-employment (Gaviria,
2004) found that under-employment(working less than full time) had decreased. Finally,Amarante and
Arim (2005) investigatedthe effect of the changes in legislationon average salaries and found positive
effects.




''' Other occupational positions (Domestic employees, working for oneself and working in the home
without pay) do not guarantee social security coverage for health and pension nor the payment of
unemployment benefits.


                                                   86

NacionalTraining Program SENA -
27. With relation to the SENA, the National Government has been developinga plan to put into action
some important changes, not only in the operationand internal structure of the institution,but also in
the trainingmarket.

28. Decrees 249 and 250 of 2003 promoted the modernization and the strengthening of SENA's
training centers, granted the organizationgreater autonomy and accessto the field in order to increase
their relevanceand coverage,which is what localjob marketsrequire.

29. These results led to the adoption of a job training scheme based on training by areas using the
modalities of entrepreneurship and possibility, SENA managed to substantially increase its share of
training, particularly vocational training. Altogether, the institution increased its share of training to
1,142,798 in 2002 (176,164 corresponded to degree-based training and 966,634 to vocational) to
3,853,352 in 2005 (355,613 longand 3,497,739short).

30. In referenceto learning, the impact of the labor reform is evident in the substantial increasein the
number of trainees with company contracts that went from 33,337 in 2003 to 75,494 in 2005. In this
lastyear, only 27.5% of traineeswere linkedto companies by organizationsother than SENA.

31. SENA provides training for labor insertionand re-insertionof populationsegments that are acutely
facing the adverseeffects of the economiccrises or that have special personalcharacteristics,such as
the vulnerable population, within which are those displaced, handicapped, demobilized, in old-age,
indigenous,women headof householdsand unemployedyouth.

32. SENA trained more than 54,000 people in 2002 and more than 527,000 in 2005. Also, it managed
the operation of the fourth meeting of the Youth in Action Program (Familias en Accion) and the
extension of the rural Youth Program (Programa Jovenes), which was developed by the training
centers.The first programgraduated254,578 young peoplefrom the first two layersof the ruralsector,
meanwhile99,916 young people graduated in the second program. The efforts of the organizationto
contributeto reducing unemploymentthrough their actionsare demonstratedbythe fact that morethan
27% of their budgetis investedin the unemployed population.

33. SENA has managed to improve the job search information system used by both employers and
employees. All parts of the system can be made virtual, including the sign-up and the request and
receipt of information, which makes the information more agile and easily accessed. In addition, it is
importantthat the different public and private informationsystems function in a similar way and allow
workers, companies,institutionsand the public in generalthe use of reliable and complete information
to improve labor relations and the development of human resources. The percentage of people who
found ajob throughthis meanswent from 40.7 % in 2002 to 47% in 2005.

34. In reference to the training market, the National Council of Economic and Social Policy (Consejo
Nacional de Politica Econdmica y Social, Conpes) approved the 2003 document 081, which
establishedthe transition plan for the consolidation of the National System of Job Training (Sistema
Nacional de Formacidn para el Trabajo, SNFT) into different components in such a way that the
allocation of resources and functions is more transparent and efficient: regulation of the system,
accreditationof organizationsand work training programs, relevanceof the training, regulationof work
competencies,certificationof work competenciesand provisionof job training.

35. The Ministryof the Social Protectionand the Ministry of Educationare responsiblefor the working
together to assign functions and implementthe different componentsfor which they have developedan
Action Plan that describes the approval of the System's training model and the elaborationof a rough
draft of the decree through which it is hoped that incentiveswill be generatedfor the inclusionof those
who provide training within SNFT and the quality and coverage of users will be increased. Also,
through this Action Plan they are defining the actions and competencies of each organization in their
areas of interestwith the purposeof adapting solid criteria (a product of the assistance of specialized
groups from each Ministry)for the developmentof the other components.



                                                    87

36. SENA attempted to strengthen the National System of Job Training, SNFT, and advanced in the
implementationand fortification of the following processes: Regulation, Evaluation    - certificationofjob
competenciesand in the programs of technical education; and the recognitionofjob trainingprograms.
In order to support the process of regulating labor competencies, up until December of 2005, 59
discussion sessions have been carried out for the sectors of service, industry, primary, productive
chains and for cross-sectional areas. These instances of national accord integrated by unions,
businessmen, workers, the government, educational organizations and research and technology
development centers have elaborated 1,771 norms of labor competencies through their technical
teams, which correspondto 371 degree programs. As far as the recognitionof programsdifferent from
those from the SENA, in December of 2003 73 programs were recognized, whereas in December of
2005 there were only 210 programs.

Family CompensationAssociations

37. The Labor Reform Law (Law 789 of 2002) redefines the competence conditions of the Family
Compensation Associations (Cajas de Compensaci6n Familiar, CCF,) extending its programs and
diversifying its portfolio of social services. Thus, the CCF is in charge of the administrationof the Fund
for the Promotion of Employment and the Protectionfrom Unemployment(Fondo para el Foment0del
Empleo y Protecci6n al Desempleo, FONEDE), which includes unemployment subsidy programs,
micro-credit programs and training for labor market insertion. Soon, with the expeditionof Decree 827
of 2003 those areas related to the administration and management of FONEDE resources will be
regulated. Later, Decree 2340 of August 19, 2003 was sent, which regulatedthe conditionsof access
to credit resources and measures to access FONEDE benefits. Following that, decree 586 of 2004
modifies decree 2340 of 2003 inthe area relatedto measuresto access FONEDEbenefits.

38. On the other hand, from the 2003 the execution of FONEDE resources have increasedto $96,904
million in 2005, which were distributedto the following programs:

2. Health Reforms


40. The objectives in health are concordantwith the policiesof social security and protection,of which
the main objectives are to increasethe coverage of social security and protection policies, and attend
to the needsof the morevulnerablepopulationgroups. Inthe SGSSS, the extensionof coveragein the
subsidized regime maintains the premise of concurrencewith local and nationalresources for its co-
financing.Also it has as high-priorityobjectivesthe country's publichealthgoals.

(i) Health Insurance Coverage

41. As far as health insurance coverage is concerned, the alternatives include the transformation to
demand-based subsidiesfrom those that are supply-based, particularlythe General InsuranceSystem
(Sistema General de ParticipacionesSGP). This process is defined by Article 54 of Law 812 of 2003
(NationalDevelopmentPlan). Inaccordancewith the implementationof the Programof reorganization,
redesign and modernizationof public hospitals (see paragraphs 53 and 54), the Nation managed to
extend coverage to nearly 2.7 million people from 2004 to 2005. It is estimated that at minimum 2
millionnewpeoplewill be enrolledin the subsidizedregimebetween2006 and 2010.

(ii)PriorityActions for Public Health: VaccinationCoverage

42. In the matterof public health,the country begunimplementinghealth policiesfor aspects relatedto
sexual and reproductive health (maternal health and adolescent pregnancy, family planning and
HIV/AIDS, among others) and the improvement in vaccination coverage through the Comprehensive
Immunization Program (Programa Ampliado de Inmunizaciones, PAI). Additionally, the country is
working to best define the goalsfor the following areas: diseasestransmittedbyvectors, maternaland
infant mortality, coherence with international commitments defined within the framework of the
MillenniumDevelopment Goals, the Childhoodand Youth CountryPlanand the food securitypolicy.

43. Of all the high-priority public health actions, the main goal is the attainment and sustainability of
useful vaccination coverage of more than 95% of all minors less than 5 years of age in the biological
Comprehensive Immunization Program. In order to reach this goal, the country will provide the
resources necessary in the General Budgetof the Nationto acquirethe biologicalagentsfor each use,
to assure their suitable distribution and conservation and to develop the necessarystrategies achieve
full vaccinationcoverage.




                                                        89

44. In order to achieve useful vaccinationcoverage, accordingto the National Development Plan2002
- 2006, the strategy of the countryis to concentrate its efforts in the achievementof usefulcoveragefor
each annual cohort of children under 1 year old, ensuring that at least 90% of those born every year
receive the completevaccination scheme for their age, in accordancewith the technical specifications
of the PAL These actions, complemented with additional operative strategies (campaigns, leaflets,
coordinated operations with the private sector, and monitoringof coverage, among others) will prevent
those children over 1 year from falling behind in immunizations,and useful vaccinationcoveragewill be
attained as reflected by complete schemes of vaccination based on age (for those younger than 5
years of age). In the last term, the Nation has guaranteed the necessary resources in the PGN that
allow them to have a sufficient supply of biologicalagents and an adequate distribution of said agents.
In this sense, the country makes advances in the renovation and preparation of the cold network to
guarantee the qualityof the biologicalagents untilthey are used.

45. Along with the sector strategies for the achievement of useful vaccination coverage, work is being
done to coordinate with the education sector and the ICBF to obtain contributions from education
establishmentsand the institutionsthat care for minors, in the identificationof the infant populationthat
is not covered or is incompletelycovered byvaccinations. With this intention, decree 2287 of 2003 was
sent, establishing that the educationand health/well-beingestablishments must notify parentsor tutors
when the minor child does not have the infant health membership card or when hislher vaccination
schedule is incomplete for hidher age, with the intentionthat the child would then receive the missing
immunizations. Also, they must formally notifythe Local Health Directorate,or the Municipalor District
government, so that the fulfillment of this right is guaranteed.

(iii) Restructuring,redesign and modernizationof public hospitals

46. In developing Conpes 3204, the Ministryof Social Protection has carried out actions that allow for
the implementationof the National HealthServices Policy(Politica Nacionalde Prestacidnde Servicios
en Salud). In this sense, a document was sent that defines the main axes of action of the policy
(accessibility, quality and efficiency in the provision of health services), consolidates the program of
reconstruction,redesign and modernizationof public hospitals (at the moment a credit inthe amount of
US$50 million is being developed with the Inter-American Development Bank to continue with a
second phase) and it advances unquestionably in the implementation of Quality Assurance System
(Sistemade Garantiade Calidad)for the provisionof health services.

47. To date, the results of the reconstruction, redesign and modernizationof public hospitals program
can be synthesized as follows: 1) 24 departments have service provision networks, 2) 88 health
service lending institutions, in 13 departments, 3) increase in the production of ambulatory(24.5%) and
surgical services (19.4%), 4) reduction of lower-level jobs by 37.1%, 5) reduction of personnel
expenses, as well as total expenses, in order to achieve balance and financial sustainability, and a
decrease in the deficit of 84.8% and 6) reduction of the deficit, quantified in nine departments (92%
estimated). It is important to indicate that the results of the program will be clearer and more
demonstrable18 monthsafter the program is implemented.

48. Given the above mentioned, the actions to follow are: 1) to complement the interventions made
with a goal to overcome financial imbalance and guaranteesustainability in the medium term and 2) to
integrallyimplementthe provisionof health services policy.


fiv)Ensurina QualitvHealth Services

49. In order to create favorable conditions for the recipient of health services in the SGSSS, the
Ministry of the Social Protection has advanced in the development of regulatory norms on quality. In
this sense, the Ministry sent the norms to be reviewed by Health Services Lending Institutions
(InstitutcionesPrestadoras de Servicios de Salud, Decree 2309 of 2002) and by the Administrators of
the Subsidized Regime (Administradoras del R6gimen Subsidiado, Decree 515 of 2004); the Ministry
also made advances in the preparation of a similar norm for the Health Promoting Entities in the
contributing regime. This way, and in coordination with the National Superintendent of Health, it will
have to orient its efforts to the monitoringand control of the agents affected by these norms and in the
generation of usefulpublic informationfor the usersof the system.

                                                      90

3. Colombian Instituteof FamilvWelfare ICBF
                                          -
50. The ICBF advances in the implementationof institutionalchanges derivedfrom their reconstruction
and from the definitionof internal co-financingand investmenttargeting policies. In coordinationof the
Ministry of the Social Protection, and as director of the National Family Welfare System (Sistema
Nacional de Bienestar Familiar), the ICBF, works in pursuit of the approval of Law 085 of 2005, the
Law of childhood and adolescence,which is being reviewedby the Senate, and the formulation of the
First Childhood Nutritional and Food Security policies (with support from the National Planning
Department). The process by which these policies have been constructed has been in alliance and
participationwith institutionalactors, Ministries,community-basedentities, NGOs, universities,and the
public sector, among others. The policyframework for the First Childhood project is expected in mid-
2006 and the policyshould be enacted bythefollowingyear.

51. On the other hand, the ICBF has been able to attain agreements with local organizations to
combine resources. It has elaborated the co-financing scheme for programs using payroll tax
resources, resources from community-based entities and other resources (Family Compensation
Associations and NGOs). The objectiveof the co-financing is to promotethe infant and family policies
being developed by the country. The achievements in the co-management and co-financing of
resources have mainlybeen observed in the extensionof coverageand improvementin service quality
in schoolcafeterias, risingfor the year 2005 to $70,026,868,092(allocatedby Law 715 of 2001).

52. In relation to the creation and inclusion of childhood and adolescent themes in the territories, a
team was put together with representativesfrom the Office of the Judge Advocate General, ICBF and
UNICEF, for the development and follow up of the strategy "Municipalities and Departments for
Children and Adolescents", which focuses its work around eight (8) priorities to guarantee a dignified
life to children and adolescents: maternal health, infant health, nutrition, sexual and reproductive
health, potable water and basic sanitation, civil registry, education and re-establishmentof rights that
have been violated. 23 departmentalforums were held, with the attendance of the respectivemayors,
to developthis strategy. Also the book was published:"Municipalitiesand departmentsfor childrenand
adolescents"  - directionsforthe communityaction, whose object is to providea tool to orient and guide
the efforts of mayors and governors and their work parties, in the planningand implementationof the
actions necessary to guarantee a dignified life to children and adolescents. 1047 of 1098 mayors
signedthe commitmentpactfor childhoodand adolescence.

At the same time, the process continues to promote the creation and operation of the Social Policy
Council (Consejos de Politica Socia, CPS) in the municipalitiesof the country; there were 563 CPS in
2005 (SIGOB goals), hoping that these develop local situation-based diagnostics with social
participation.

53. In 2005 the childhood breakfast program reached 1,006,074 children in 1,053 municipalities and
5,270 potentialusers were identified using the informationfrom the new Sisben. Also in the allocation
of shares for the National Feeding Program for the Older Adults, "Juan Luis LondoAo De la Cuesta,"
and for the displaced, information was used from the new SISBEN. Up to December of 2005, the
programserved 288,212 older adults.Also for the programmingof the 2006 Socialand FinancialGoals
a table with information from the new SISBEN was sent at the end of 2005 to the Regions, with
information broken down by municipality so that this information would be taken into account when
allocatingresourcesat the local level.

In the same way, the NationalGovernmentadvances in the elaborationof the documentthat seeks to
definethe technicalcriteria for the election of the targetinginstrumentsand actionsfor the use of such
instruments, in order to improve the targeting of public social expenditures and to institutionalizethe
technicalcapacity and transparencyfor the measurementand the monitoringof povertyindicators.

54. Equally, the Government works to strengthen the institutional capacity for the pursuit and
evaluationof the management, results and impacts of its main investment programs.As of December
2005,the InformationSystemwas initiatedto supportto the ERP's administrativemanagementand the
analysis of requirements and design for the Information system to support management of their
mission.

                                                    91

55. Interms of evaluatingtheir main programs,the ICBF advances in the evaluation of the Program of
Breakfast for Children (Programa de Desayunos Infantiles), whose second measurement is in the
process of being analyzed. The NationalPlanningDepartmentadvancedthe publicbiddingprocess for
the impact evaluation of the program Community Well-being Homes, culminatingwith the selectionof
biddersphase.



111. EDUCACION

56. Educationis an essentialfactor for human, social and economic development and a fundamental
instrument for the construction of social equity. For that reason, it is worrisome that in spite of the
efforts made by this and the previous administrations, among them greater education expenditures,
and the undeniable advances in coverage, quality and efficiency, Colombia has not managed to
universalize access to a basic education of quality. The lack of education constitutes one of the
substantialfactors behindthe persistenceof inequalityand concentrationof opportunitiesamong those
morewell off.

57. The coverage and the quality of education are the lead determining factors to assuring the
competitiveness of a country. Social and economic development are directly associated with the
increase of productivity,which depends on a balance between improvementsin science, technology
and innovationand the increasein educationand the abilities of the laborforce. Experienceshows that
the countries that manage to develop ordered interactions,with linear transitions, and both fast and
balanced, obtain acceleratedand more sustainable increases in productivityand growth. This implies
the need to promotepoliciesthat guaranteelinear and gradual increases in coverageand qualityat the
different levelsof education.

58. The strategy of the EducationRevolutionis to respondto the necessitiesof coverage, quality and
efficiency that the countryrequiresto attain better social and economic developmentconditions and to
improvethe qualityof lifeof the population.

59. The policyof extendingcoverage in preschool, basic and middle education is directedat elevating
gross coverage from 82% to 92% with the creation of 1.5 million educative shares, giving special
attentionto the most vulnerable populationand lookingfor greater equity in service provision.This will
be obtainedbymeans of the implementationof severalcomplementary efforts:

60. Strengtheningthe process of reorganizationof district, departmentaland municipal organizations
and the educational institutions in order to obtain a better balance and equity in the distribution of
physical, human and financial resources and the optimal use of the installed capacity. The
developmentof this mechanism should result in the generation of 800,000 new shares. Additionally,
the teacher student ratio has been raised from 2002-2005 from 2.78 students per teacher in public
schools, thus increasingfrom 26.7 to 29.48. This is proof of the efficiency achieved by the education
sector thanks to the processof reorganizationof human,physicaland financial resources.

61. Creation of 640,000 new education allocations from the use of resources from the National
Exemption Fund (Fondo Nacional de Regalias, FNR) and other additional resources. With resources
from the FNR, the education of 23,965 children was financed in 2003, 34,855 children in 2004 and
43,326 children in 2005. At the same time, with additional resourcestotaling $150 billion in 2005, the
coverage extension project was financed, which reached more than 220,000 children and young
people. In2006,additionalresources in the amount of $170 billionwere appropriated.

62. Extensionof coverage and improvement in the quality of educationthrough the implementationof
the "Educationfor RuralSector Project (Proyectode Educaci6npara el Sector Rural, PER)financed
                                       I'
by the World Bank through an investment loan. This project develops innovativeeducation models of
qualityand applicabilityfor ruralareas.They are beingimplemented:

At the moment, the evaluation of the PER is being completed and conversations between the
government and the World Bank have taken place to advance the proceedingsof a second loan. The
second loan depends on the preliminary results of the evaluation, as it relates to the extension of
coverageand efficiencyin service provision.

63. Regulationof the entrance exam to become a teacher was undertakenvia the passage of Decree
3391of 2003.274,815 peopleappearedto take the test to become a teacher.

64. With respect to higher education, the National Government will promote equitable access
implementingthree mechanismsfor the retentionand incorporationof 400,000 students:

65. The Program of Quality Access to Higher Education (Programa de Acceso con Calidad a la
EducacionSuperior, ACCES), backed by resourcesfrom a World Bank loan in the amount of US$200
million, will create and strengthen financing schemes to benefit students with low incomes and high
academic achievement.       This program also establishes incentives for the improvement of the
education quality. With this program, 74,564 credits have been approved (26,014 in 2003, 26,289 in
2004 and 22.261 in 2005) and 59,201 credits were legalized (21,080 in 2003, 20,307 in 2004 and
17.814 in 2005).

66. Modernization and improvementof the managementof the public universities,with the objectiveof
increasing the efficiency in the use of physical, human and financial resources. This strategy has
allowed the creationof 211,889 newallocations(34,858 in 2003, 69,045 in 2004 and 107,986 in 2005).

67. Promotionof technical and technological education. In 2003 decree 2216 of Law 749 established
the requirementsfor the organizationof technical and technologicaleducation in cycles. Educationby
cycles allows students to learn in a sequentialand complementarymanner. At the same time, in 2003
the Regional Centers of Higher Education(Centros Regionalesde Educacion Superior, CERES) were
created, which aims to respond to the demand for higher education in zones separated from the
country. To date, 45 CERES are in operation. On the other hand, with resourcesfrom the multilateral

                                                 93

bank in the amount of US$25 millionthe Technicaland TechnologicalEducationStrengthening project
was financed,whose primarygoal is to increaseand strengthenthe supply of academic programs.

68. In order to improve the quality of the education, the National Government will offer support to
community-based organizations and the public schools that are in the process of institutional
improvement and management to assure that the students develop basic competencies, as
professionals, workers and citizens. For this purpose, between 2002 and 2005, 801,041 tests were
given in mathematicslanguage, science, socialstudies and citizenshipto students fifth and ninthgrade
in 90% of the municipalitiesof the country. Based on the results of thesetests the publicschools have
elaborated improvement plans; to date, 6,062 public schools in 77 communities have improvement
plans.

69. Also, the basicstandardsof math, language and citizenshipwere developed, and the first voluntary
evaluationof performance for principalsand teachers was carried out in 2003. The number of people
evaluatedreached97,153.

70. Conversely, in higher education, the accreditationof high qualitywas granted to 207 programsof
higher education and 2,991 programs received a qualified accreditation (with minimum conditions).
Quality of higher education was evaluated by the Quality Examinations for Higher Education (Los
Examinacionesde Calidadde la Educacidn Superior, ECAES) by evaluatingthe volunteer graduating
students in their lastyear in 55 basiccentersof knowledge.

71. The last program of the education revolution seeks the improvement of the efficiency of the
education sector. Thus, the objective is the modernizationof the administrationand the management
of the sector at the national, departmental and municipal levels. It is with this intention that four
mechanismshave been developed orientedto improve the productivity,efficiencyand transparencyof
the sector, and to assure the quality of investments: i) institutional modernizationof the Ministry of
National Education by means of the 2003 decree 2230 that gave origin to its new administrative
structure; ii) modernizationof the departmentaland municipal entities; currently, the 78 secretaries of
education are making advancements in some aspect of the modernization; iii) agreement on
management and performance plans for an efficient use of resources; and iv) development of the
education sector's informationsystem. The Ministryof National Education(MEN) has implementedthe
new national information system for higher education (Nuevo Sistema Nacional de Educacidn
Superior, SNIES) and already has results from the Labor Market study, which offers information on
graduates of highereducationand the behavior of the labor market.

72. With respect to the information system for basic and middle education, the MEN developed and
implementedthe module to capture enrollment information, and with the aid of the DNP it developed
the directory of official educational establishments(schools). At the moment, MEN is working on the
designof the personneland payrollmodules.


IV. TRANSPARENCY,SOCIAL MONITORINGAND EVALUATION

73. In a context of significant fiscal restrictions, the national government has proposedto modernize
public administration to assure that the objectives of the government, and especially those of social
policy, are obtained with effectiveness, efficiency and transparency.This implies the strengtheningof
managerial instruments to orient public management towards the achievement of results and the
maximizationof program impacts on the lives of the population. Thus, it is crucial to incorporate new
practicesthat includecitizens in the differentstagesof the administrationof the State.

74. In within this framework that the government has proposed to carry out a reform of the National
System of Evaluation of Results (Sistema Nacional de Evaluacidn de Resultados, SINERGIA).
Although this organization has contributed to introducing in Colombia the practice of results-based
management, it requires adjustments to make it an instrument able to improve the efficiency and
qualityof public expenditures,as well as the effectiveness and impact of the policies and interventions
of the State. This implies making the evaluation of main public programs a permanent practice, in
order to know the causality between the results and the interventions, to determine if these


                                                      94

interventionsare excellentand cost-effective,and to promotethe process of defining policiesbasedon
evidence, stimulatingthe renderingof accountsand the continuous learningof the State.

75. Consequently, the reform of the System is based on three aspects: i) strengtheningof the pursuit
of results, focusing on achievements as opposed to specific goals, and their ties to the budgeted
resources used; ii) the activationof the targeted evaluationscomponent; and iii) the incorporationof a
transparency component and rendering of accounts, to assure the availability of monitoring and
evaluation information, and with it to contribute to an effective rendering of accounts on the
performanceof the nationalgovernment, which allowsfor the operationof effectivesocial control.

76. The periodicaccomplishmentof targetedevaluations,especiallyof social programs,is fundamental
to determine and to quantify the effects that the programs have on their beneficiaries, as well as
establish if these are the most efficient interventions as compared to other actions, given the
investments made. Thus, they become tools for ensuringthat the allocationof public resourcescan be
made through effective and efficient programsfor the fight against povertyand the formation of human
and socialcapital.

77. The component of targeted evaluations is developed based on an evaluation plan defined by the
Inter-sectorialEvaluation Committee (Comite lntersectorialde Evaluacion)and approved by Conpes.
The programs, policiesand organizationsthat are the object of targetedevaluations(with emphasison
social programs) will be selected in accordance with the following criteria: i) the amount of public
resourcesinvolved, ii) the size and characteristicsof the affected population, iii) the importancefor the
sector; iv) the innovative character of the program or policy; and v) the potentialto apply and replicate
the lessonsderivedfrom the evaluation.

78. In addition to the proposed institutional scheme, the Government is working toward developing
additional mechanisms to assure institutional conditions that would make carrying out evaluations a
permanent practice. The mechanisms include the incorporation of legal provisions that obligate
compliance with the evaluationplan and the developmentof results monitoring in accordancewith the
methodologiesof Sinergia.

79. Conversely, a scheme has been developedof disseminationand surrenderof accounts, by which
everyone can know the results of the monitoring and evaluationscarried out by Sinergia. The scheme
uses the mainchannels of disseminationwith ample circulation,such as commercials,institutionaland
community means of communication, audio-visual, discussion forums, and electronic distribution of
information.

80. The scheme has been designedtaking into account the experienceof the program Bogota Como
Vamos ("Bogota, How are We Doing?"), as well as other national and international programs of this
type, which have proven to be effective in fulfillment of this objective. Similarly, the government,
through the DNP, this working to developan alliance with the organizationColombiaLider ("Colombia
Leader") program, which is led by the private sector and civil society organizations (Fedesarrollo,
Magazine Week, Caracol Radio, Asobancaria and Fundacion Restrepo Boat), and which has as its
objectivethe monitoring and evaluationof povertyreductionpolicies and the inequalityof the National
Government.This scheme will guarantee the transparency and the sustainabilityof these policies, as
well as promotethe participationof civilsociety inthe developmentof the Country.

81. An auditingcomponent(Rendicionde Cuentas) is working on developinginstitutionalnorms in this
area. Conpes, alongwith the Programto FightCorruption (Programade Luchacontra la Corrupcibn))
of the Vice-presidencyof the Republic, has developeda rough draft of this component, which attempts
to delineate policy actions at the local and national levels. Additionally, the government is defining an
auditing law in Congress, which is being reviewed and discussed by the Government and the First
Commissionof the Legislature(CornisionPrimerrade la Cgmara).

82. Also, the Government, through the DNP and to commemorate 10 years of SINERGIA, carried out
in September of 2004, the seminar "Why evaluate public expenditures?"with two primary goals: i) to
show the value, importance and feasibility of evaluation in situations of fiscal restriction of the type
Colombia is currently experiencing; and ii) to learn international lessons on the design and
institutionalizationof periodic impact evaluations and the monitoring of results. The forum includedthe

                                                   95

participation of academic and international public officials who are experts in evaluation, as well as
national specialist, and aimed to generate a public debate between government officials, academics
and those in other sectors interestedin the value of evaluation for Colombia. All this with the purpose
of promoting a culture of evaluation that allows for the strengthening of the proposed reform of
SINERGIA.

83. As an integral part of the dissemination strategy and with the interestto continue with the process
initiated with the 2004 seminar, in February of 2006 an international seminar was held on "Fiscal
Transparency: Budgeting for results and quality of public spending". The objectiveof the forum was to
disclosethe fiscal concept of transparency and to discuss the utilityof the results-basedbudgeting as a
managerial tool that permitsan improvement intransparency. The discussions were structuredthrough
four areas of complementary analyses: (i) reforms to the budgetary institutions and results-based
budgeting, (ii) the results of the reforms in fiscal performance in accordance with international
experience, (iii) national and international experience in results-based budgeting, and (IV) results-
based budgeting in local and regional governments. Like the previous seminar, national and
internationalexpertson the subjectwere present and actively participated.
