ANNEX111:FUNDRELATIONSNOTE

Attached is a macroeconomic assessment from IMF Staff. Please note that the second review of the
Stand ByArrangement was completed onJune 12th.


                              Colombia- Assessment Letterto the WorldBank
                                        Statement bytheIMFStaff
                                                June 7,2006

In April2005, the Executive B o d of the Fund approved an l8-month Stand-By Arrangement
(precautionar);) inanamountequivalent to SDR405 million(35 percentof quotaonanannualbasis). The
authorities are using this arrangement to provide a transparent policy framework during the current
political cycle andintend to exit fromformalFundsupport when this arrangement ends onNovember 2,
2006. The first review under the arrangement was completed inOctober, 2005 and the second review is
expected to be completed on a lapse of time basis onJune 12,2006. Colombia has no o u t s t a n k credit
fromtheFundandhas acceptedthe obligations of Article VIII, Sections 2,3, and4.

In 2005, performance under the programwas strong. Real GDP grew by over 5 percent in 2005,
reflecting strong domestic demand, particularlyinvestment. Consumer price inflationslowed to below 5
percent. The public finances improved significantly as the combined public sector achieved an overall
balance of zero, owing inpart to temporary factors. Incontrast, the external current account deficit rose
to 1.6 percent of GDP, higher than expected. This was financed byhtgher net foreign direct investment
that was partiallyoffset bya buildup of net foreignassets bythe publicsector. Net international reserves
reached uS$14.7 billion(128 percent of short-term external debt), as the central bank purchasedforeign
exchange to slow the appreciation of the peso. Structural reforms advanced. All quantitative performance
criteria andmanystructuralbenchmarks were observed.

The 2006 program is sound and consistent with the authorities' medium-term policy framework Real
GDP growth would taper off to 4.5 percent in 2006 and to 4.0 percent a year in2007 and beyond.
Inflation is targeted to fall to 4% percent in2006 and then to 2-4 percent over the medium term. The
external sector would remain strong, although private capital inflows and declining oil production would
raise the current account deficit starting in2007. Public debt would decline to 41 percent of GDP by
2010, as envisaged inthe program

The authorities have lowered the target for the combined public sector (CDS) deficit to 1.5 percent of
GDP in2006, from2.0 percent previouslyprogrammed. The weaker fiscal positionrelative to 2005 is
explained bya change inthe accounting treatment of interest expenses (which raises the reported deficit
by 0.6-0.8 percent of GDP) and increases in spending on social projects, oil exploration and
infrastructure. InJuly2006, the authorities intend to submit a 2007 budget consistent with a CPS deficit
of 1.7 percent of GDP.

The authorities intendto deepen s            d reforms. Their strategy is to concentrate first on submitting
reforms of the tax code and intergovernmental transfers, which are structural benchmarks under the
program Theywillcontiuue withreforms of the public enterprise sector andrevenue earmarking, butsee
no needfor another roundof pensionreformat this stage. They are also preparing reforms to strengthen
creditor rights, promote universalbankingandgive more independence to the financial superintendency,

The central bank's monetary policy is consistent with achievement of the inflation target. Inlate April
2006, the central bank raised its policy interest rate by 25 basis points to 6.25 percent. The peso has
depreciated vis-bis the U.S. dollar since late February 2006, inresponse to &her        interest rates inthe
United States, and the central bank sold almost uS$600 million inApril and Mayunder its intervention
rule to limit volatility. Net international reserves are projected to rise to uS$15.2 billion by end-2006
(about 150 percent of short-termexternal debt).


                                                    102

Inthe staff's view, the authorities' policystrategyhasbeensuccessful.Bystrengtheningfiscal policyand
effectively managing the inflation targeting framework, the authorities have taken advantage of the
favorable global economyto strengthen confidence further. This has enabled the economyto grow at a
healthy pace, leading to declines inunemployment and poverty. The external current account deficit is
relatively low, supported by rapid growth in exports even though the peso has strengthened in recent
years. The prospects for continued macroeconomic stabilityand sustained growth over the mediumterm
are favorable.




                                                   103
